  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_17505c1d-f25a-4744-9645-23ba0af32d79'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_407401150" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/407401150" />
    <a title="Abby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12495474-abby"><img alt="Abby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405127516p2/12495474.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/407401150?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abby" href="/user/show/12495474-abby">Abby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12495474-abby?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12495474-abby?shelf=best-heroines">best-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12495474-abby?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12495474-abby?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer407401150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2647435140432948256">You know, one of the best feelings in the world is going to bed and knowing that the next morning the next book in one of your favorite series is going to be on your kindle. But that's second-to-best to actually reading the thing.  <br/><br/> Sentimentality aside, I loved this book! <br/><br/>  The characters are back in full swing. Tory is either first or second on my all time favorite charcters list. <br/><br/>    I began to feel uneasy about Ben. His feud with Jason escalates to the point where the Virals have to drag him</span>
  <span id="freeText2647435140432948256" style="display:none">You know, one of the best feelings in the world is going to bed and knowing that the next morning the next book in one of your favorite series is going to be on your kindle. But that's second-to-best to actually reading the thing.  <br /><br /> Sentimentality aside, I loved this book! <br /><br />  The characters are back in full swing. Tory is either first or second on my all time favorite charcters list. <br /><br />    I began to feel uneasy about Ben. His feud with Jason escalates to the point where the Virals have to drag him away. He makes stupid decisions. He gets drunk once and admits to getting drunk another time. But by the end of the novel, he makes the right choice.  <br /><br /> Kit...oh Kit. He's so clueless it's sortof adorable when he says,   "But if you're up to something, know that I'm ready. The days of Kit the Clueless are over. I'm watching you like...a really good watcher of things. An owl, maybe?"<br /><br />   Usually, having books spoiled for me doesn't ruin the book. But this time it did. The twist at the end? You'll never see it coming, and like the other books, I don't think you'll see the antagonist--the twisted Gamemaster--coming.   Despite her problems with the Virals, Tory also juggles cotillion (is that how you spell it?) and Whitney. For all the years I've been reading this series, I was always hoping that Tory would stand up to Whitney and to tell her shut up. When she finally does, her relationship with Whitney improves to some extent. Whitney, it turns out, isn't quite as brainless as we all thought. Well, at least she has the decency to feel sorry about her actions.<br /><br />Favorite moments:  <br /><br />"CANNONBALL!"<br /><br />"Always trapped!" Sheldon actually stamped a foot. "Always underground! If we get out of here,  I'm moving to a high-rise on a mountaintop. Penthouse! And y'all ain't invited!"<br /><br />Tory calling Kit "Dad" for the first time.</span>

The whole recombinant DNA thing is back! I used to <i>love</i> the Maximum Ride series, but then it turned into romantic mush. Anyway, I like the recombinant DNA idea because it gives the characters powers without turning the book into fantasy. <div id="review_477332892" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/477332892" />
    <a title="Sophie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15464824-sophie"><img alt="Sophie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/477332892?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie" href="/user/show/15464824-sophie">Sophie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15464824-sophie?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15464824-sophie?shelf=the-point-challenge">the-point-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer477332892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer161850657908909920">There is NO POSSIBLE WAY anyone could give this anything less than 5 stars. It is just <i>impossible</i>. This book was the breath-taking, nerve racking, mind blowing third book in the Virals series.<br/>May I repeat.<br/>NO POSSIBLE WAY.<br/><br/>So, with that off my chest, I will begin my review.<br/><br/>Oh. My. Freaking. GOD.<br/><br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ When I read that the third <i>Virals</i> book was about a bomb, I almost died. I <i>needed</i> this book immediately, and I had to wait another <i>freaking year</i> for it to be released. So I tortured myself wi</span></span>
  <span id="freeText161850657908909920" style="display:none">There is NO POSSIBLE WAY anyone could give this anything less than 5 stars. It is just <i>impossible</i>. This book was the breath-taking, nerve racking, mind blowing third book in the Virals series.<br />May I repeat.<br />NO POSSIBLE WAY.<br /><br />So, with that off my chest, I will begin my review.<br /><br />Oh. My. Freaking. GOD.<br /><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ When I read that the third <i>Virals</i> book was about a bomb, I almost died. I <i>needed</i> this book immediately, and I had to wait another <i>freaking year</i> for it to be released. So I tortured myself with teasers, discussions and speculations. <br />How would it end?<br />What could the twist be?<br />It ended up being nothing and yet everything like what I expected it to be.<br />It was everything like I thought it would be because I knew it would be awesome. Because, come on, it is <i>Kathy Reichs</i> writing it. How on <i>earth</i> could it go wrong? :)<br /><br />- Basic Storyline - <br /><br />Tory Brennan is out on Loggerhead with her fellow pack mates (read <i>Virals</i> and <i>Seizure</i>) Hi, Shelton and Ben. Hi introduces the group to "geocaching" - which, by the way, I participate in and is <i>incredibly</i> fun! - and they dig the one on Loggerhead. This discovery results only ina frustrating box and a cryptic message. Little did they know that this would lead them on a potentially fatal dance with a child-like maniac. It is revealed to them that they are playing with a mass murderer. The "GameMaster" has planted a bomb somewhere, and is leaving encrypted clues and an unidentified body in his wake for the Virals to find and use to divert a mass murder. <br />But, they can't go to the police.<br />They can't tell their parents.<br />They can't tell their friends.<br />Because if they do, everyone will die.<br />While struggling with cotillion début balls, a suspicious Chance and Tripod, mysterious tensions between friends and the inevitable moving in of Whitney, Tory must some how also figure out the GameMaster's puzzle and save hundreds, if not thousands, of lives.<br />As the story progresses, Tory is presented with the confusing dilemma of Jason and Ben. Silent, and sometimes physical, tension accompanies the encounters between the two, and little does Tory know that she is the cause of it.<br /><br />In the end, Tory is forced to tell Jason and Chance of the bomb, therefore breaking the rules of the Game. The consequences will be fatal. They have discovered where the bomb is.<br />It's hidden at the Cotillion Début Ball. <br />They are faced with a choice. <br />Either they can leave the deadly gas bomb to kill the hundreds of people attending the ball - or they can sacrifice themselves.<br />But they are Virals.<br />And Virals don't get beaten.<br />Knocking out Jason and distracting Chance, they flare, and save themselves.<br />When they emerge from the basement, dirty, coughing, and injured with suits and dress torn, they cover it up by saying they tripped in the dark.<br />They didn't say that they just stopped a bomb from killing everyone.<br />And the debs are none the wiser.<br /><br />But one problem remains.<br />Who is the Gamemaker?<br /><br />Proceeding to use their skills of deduction, they hunt down the man in the midst of a hurricane. Together, as a pack, they hunt him down and capture him. But not before the Gamemaker makes a final taunt.<br /><br /><i>"Tell Ben thankyou. I've never worked with a partner before. It made this game so much more exciting than others, being able to get so close-"</i><br /><br />It was Ben.<br />Ben was involved.<br />It wasn't until they were safely in the Charlestone Hospital that Ben explained.<br />He did it because he wanted to impress Tory. No one was supposed to get hurt - it was supposed to be a <i>game</i>. But things got out of hand, and soon they were playing for their lives. And finally, when she asks him why he did it, he says the one thing we've wanted him to say for the past two books. The thing we've wanted, hoped, <i>needed</i> him to say.<br /><br />~ Scene from end of book ~<br /><br />"Tell me why, Ben. Why would you want to trick us in the first place?"<br />Ben stopped pacing. Looked at me directly. "Don't you know?"<br />I shook my head, confused.<br />"To impress you, Victoria Brennan." His voice cracked. "I wanted you to think I was special."<br />The words rocked me.<br /><i>Oh, Ben.</i><br />He'd started this madness... for me?<br />"You were spending all that time with Jason," Ben said softly, staring at his shoes. "Skipping around town with your new perfect guy. Cotillion <i>this.</i> Fundraiser <i>that</i>. I <i>hated</i> it. Hated <i>him</i>. When I finally told Rome, he said I needed to amaze you. Said I had to figure out a way to make you see me."<br />"I see you, Ben." I rose and grabbed his hand. "I always have. You're in my pack."<br />He pulled away. "What if being packmates isn't enough?"<br />I was speechless.<br />~ End scene ~<br /><br />Heartbreaking.<br />Convinced it was his fault, he went and told the authorities it was partly him.<br />Charges weren't pressed, but something else took hold.<br />Ben was being expelled from Bolton.<br /><br />The book ended with a scene of Chance Claybourne, in his cellar. He was putting the pieces together about Tory and her gang. About the research Karsten was doing. About what they <i>are</i>. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And then it just... finished.<br />And I was like WHAT?<br />Deadly cliffhanger. Cannot wait for book 4, whatever it will be and whenever it will be released.<br /><br />:)<br /><br />An undeniable, whole-hearted, completely earnt FIVE STARS for Kathy Reichs revolutionary forensic science, murder mystery and fantasy thriller <i>Code</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="161850657908909920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_595253986" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/595253986" />
    <a title="Mary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3076222-mary"><img alt="Mary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299283701p2/3076222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/595253986?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary" href="/user/show/3076222-mary">Mary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3076222-mary?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3076222-mary?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3076222-mary?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3076222-mary?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3076222-mary?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3076222-mary?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3076222-mary?shelf=50in2013">50in2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer595253986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13020800826609221104">Kind of mixed feelings about this one. I might have enjoyed it more if I could turn off my critical perspective and looked at it purely for its entertainment value (like I do for the Alex Rider series), but I wasn't able to for this one. Still, I'm not done with the series yet; the premise for the next book definitely intrigues me, and I've enjoyed things well enough so far to give the Reichs a second chance.<br/><br/>The good things: <br/><br/>1) The Reichs know how to write a tense and action-packed story; it was</span>
  <span id="freeText13020800826609221104" style="display:none">Kind of mixed feelings about this one. I might have enjoyed it more if I could turn off my critical perspective and looked at it purely for its entertainment value (like I do for the Alex Rider series), but I wasn't able to for this one. Still, I'm not done with the series yet; the premise for the next book definitely intrigues me, and I've enjoyed things well enough so far to give the Reichs a second chance.<br /><br />The good things: <br /><br />1) The Reichs know how to write a tense and action-packed story; it was exciting to read and had a couple of plot twists I hadn't expected, which is always enjoyable. The hurricane sequence was especially good; while not the most realistic thing to happen, it had me very much at the edge of my seat wanting to know what was next.<br /><br />2) The friendship between Tory and her three guy friends stays strong and still pretty central to the story; it's less common in YA books for girls and guys to just be friends without any romantic undertones. (Well, okay, there's a clear setup for romance with Ben, but not with Sheldon and Hi, and they're all equally important to Tory.)<br /><br />3) The setting. I just kind of love all the details about the city, the islands, the monastery they visit. Sometimes the characters end up info-dumping encyclopedia information about places in the middle of their conversations, which can be awkward, but really, that's a minor quibble.<br /><br />4) Something Ben-related that is all spoilers: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I like that his crush on Tory is finally out in the open! Tory's obliviousness to it and the way the other characters talked around it was driving me nuts. I'm less thrilled that it took until the end of the book for Ben to say anything, and even then he only spoke up because Tory was asking him point blank, but hey, at least it happened. I also like that this revelation came paired with Ben's confession about knowing the Gamemaster and his own role in setting up the Game; there's a lot of potential now for how his story might develop, when all I really expected was to go down the typical "friends turned romantic partners" path. Please don't let me down in the next book! *crosses fingers* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />The sorta okay, sorta not, maybe-it's-just-me things:<br /><br />1) The puzzles. While overall I liked them and enjoyed that they were clever enough that I wasn't able to figure them out on my lonesome, there were some glaringly easy conclusions Team Viral should have made much sooner than they did. Their slowness felt more like a plot contrivance than actual difficulty, which is just weak writing. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The most egregious has to be not recognizing that the string of letters and numbers in the (third?) clue was a chemical equation; it's less obvious in the description in the book, I guess, but the picture included in the text has "H2O" positioned at the top left of the black circle, the most natural place for people's eyes to fall (at least for Western people) because we're taught to read left to right. It strained credibility that these kids--who most of the time <i>are</i> pretty clever!--would not see that right away. Or even if they missed it, it's hard to believe that Google wouldn't figure it out when they did their first search string. Am I supposed to believe these kids don't use Google? I mean, really. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />2) The subplot with that weirdly antagonistic doctor dude. I'm sure it's setup for future books, but nothing really came of it in this story, so it felt out of place.<br /><br />The not so good things:<br /><br />1) The setup of this story's mystery/thriller bit is ludicrously convoluted and requires more than a little suspension of disbelief. (And I'm saying this about a series whose previous plot points include a <i>virus that gives humans wolf-like powers</i>, and <i> pirate treasure in the sewers beneath Charleston</i>. Yes, the plot of this story is THAT out there.) There's a revelation at the end of the story that helps mitigate its absurdity somewhat, but really, the more I think about it, the less substantial that explanation becomes. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I understand Ben was being manipulated by the Gamemaster, but come on. It's a ridiculous amount of effort for Ben to trick his friends into doing this geocache thing, making sure they buy the right stuff and find the right clues, all so he can have a moment to be clever in front of the girl he likes. Was there really no other way for him to show off his smarts to Tory? No other way to get her attention? God forbid he actually just tell her he likes her and ask her out on a date. (And actually, why would he need to trick Sheldon and Hi at all? They're written as each other's only friends, really, so I can't imagine why they wouldn't be supportive of Ben finally doing something about his crush. His decision to stay quiet about his connection to the Gamemaster, I don't like much, but I actually understand it better: when things went sideways, he basically set up camp in Denial Land and hoped he wouldn't be called on his actions. Not the most admirable thing, but definitely a realistic mistake for somebody who's never before been in a position where he's (partially) responsible for getting people hurt.) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />2) The portrayal of women and femininity in the story is starting to grate on my nerves. While I quite like Tory (especially her interest in science, her leadership skills, her intelligence, her impulsiveness that gets them out of scrapes as often as it gets them in), she only interacts with a handful of female characters and her attitude toward them--dismissive, condescending, even antagonistic at times--I find quite troubling. The High School Mean Girls is a cliche found in a lot of YA stories and this series is no exception. In the earlier books, it was mostly a tiresome but easily skimmed over part of the story--the girls didn't like Tory because she's not rich/from the right neighborhood/into feminine things like they are, and because oh-so-attractive-and-popular Jason is interested in Tory instead of them; so they're mean to her until she finally takes a stand and berates them in public for their actions, yada yada yada--but in this book, the relationship takes an uncomfortable twist. <br /><br />At the end of <i>Seizure</i>, Tory slipped up and let one of the Mean Girls, Madison, see her glowing wolf-powered eyes; Madison, understandably, is freaked out afterwards. She spends the entirety of this story cringing and cowering away from Tory, and it gets even worse when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tory tries to use her mental powers to read Madison's thoughts, an invasion that Madison can physically feel and is an immensely terrifying experience for her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. And Tory? Tory mostly seems to think that it was a bad move on her part because it made Madison even more suspicious of her and more willing to talk to Chance, who is on a quest to figure out the truth of Team Viral. She's not upset at all that she flagrantly violated Madison's privacy, in a way that actually hurt her and left her afraid and probably questioning her sanity. I'm holding out hope that in the next book, Tory gets a wake up call that what she did (is doing) is wrong. I mean, Tory's capable of it! She feels horrible about lying to Chance and making him doubt his sanity, even though <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Chance tried to kill her last book <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, so why wouldn't she feel some guilt for what she's doing to Madison? At the moment, though, Tory feels her actions are vindicated and the narrative doesn't undercut that conclusion. (I suppose I should be fair though: Tory doesn't feel much guilt about doing the same thing to her friends, even after they've explicitly told her not to, so perhaps it's too much to ask her to feel badly about how she's treating someone who once bullied her?)<br /><br />The other main female character Tory interacts with is her father's girlfriend, Whitney, and wow, does Tory dislike her. It's not that it's unrealistic for Tory to feel that way--she and Whitney value very different things, and Tory is still dealing with grief from her mother passing away, so she'd likely struggle to accept any female potentially-parental figure--but her feelings stay shallow. It's been three books now, and while there have been one or two moments where Tory has been willing to recognize that Whitney isn't a complete waste of space, most of their relationship is static: Whitney tries to get Tory to like her and Tory continues not to. There's no progression, no lasting recognition on Tory's part that Whitney is a person with value. (Whitney doesn't seem to understand Tory very well either, but at least she makes an effort.) Again, these are perhaps not inauthentic feelings for someone in Tory's position to have, but the way the Reichs write them, it feels less like characterization and more like cliche bordering on caricature.<br /><br />Additionally, it's very problematic that there's only a few other female characters in the books and Tory looks down on them all, calling them "skank" and "bimbo" in turn. In addition to perpetuating the idea that all women are catty and vicious to each other, this "Tory vs. Them" setup makes for an uncomfortable commentary on the kind of femininity valued by Tory (and the authors). People, there isn't a wrong way to be female! Liking science and hating dressing up isn't superior to wearing make-up and owning frilly things, and I wish the authors would be a little more aware of this. At the very least in the next book, can you give me a female character Tory actually <i>likes</i>?<br /><br />3) I'm also pretty done with the masculine one-upmanship between Jason and Ben over Tory's affections. Jason, dude, Tory already turned you down. Chill out and be a friend. Ben, you've got nothing to stand on until you actually man up and say something to Tory about your crush, and even then, it's not cool to be a jerk to her friends. Jealousy is not attractive. At least the narrative is with me on this point, but that's small comfort. If the Reichs weren't going to do anything novel with the whole "rival suitors" cliche, I'd have preferred for them to skip it altogether. Boooring.<br /><br />4) The Gamemaster is your cliched psychopathic villain, down to the high-pitched giggling and weirdly detailed Master Plan that our intrepid heroes just happen to stumble into. Boring and overdone. The only saving grace is that at least the Game he came up with was interesting.<br /><br /><br />Recommended mainly to people who are already invested in the series, but it could also work for anyone looking for light reading who's practiced at overlooking flaws. Appropriate for high schoolers, maybe even some older middle schoolers who wouldn't be frightened by the setup.<br /><br />(Also: how on earth do I always end up writing essays for mediocre books I could take or leave, but when it comes to write a review for ones I absolutely love, I can barely string two words together? Seriously, this review is epically long; if you made it this far, have a cookie.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13020800826609221104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Aether" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15949058-aether"><img alt="Aether" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582512795p2/15949058.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/561120343?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aether" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aether" href="/user/show/15949058-aether">Aether</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer561120343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9774646341493390200">This. Was. An. Awesome. Book.<br/>Go, Kathy Reichs! I love the whole virals thing, its enormously inventive. I still havent recoverred from this book. Read it twice in 5 hours. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Tory's debutante ball was very well written. In the next book, someone is <b> so </b> going to find out they are virals. Madison, Jason and Chance all have seen way too much. Im amazed that Kit or the other parents havent figured out something is off. Excuse me, but I would notice something weird if the same four teen</span></span>
  <span id="freeText9774646341493390200" style="display:none">This. Was. An. Awesome. Book.<br />Go, Kathy Reichs! I love the whole virals thing, its enormously inventive. I still havent recoverred from this book. Read it twice in 5 hours. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Tory's debutante ball was very well written. In the next book, someone is <b> so </b> going to find out they are virals. Madison, Jason and Chance all have seen way too much. Im amazed that Kit or the other parents havent figured out something is off. Excuse me, but I would notice something weird if the same four teens kept accomplishing freaky stuff.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><i> Whats with all this formatting stuff you have to type in? Its annoying! </i><br /><br />If you have read Virals and Seizure, you have to read this book. I recommend it for all teens who like any of the following: Mystery, Suspense, Adventure, or SciFi. This book is beyond realistic. Im one step away from going to look up parvo. This all just seems like it could actually happen. Kill me now!<br /><br />The mystery part of this book was extremly well done. There were so many hidden clues that you dont notice until you have reread this. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ben kept acting weird, but I was just like Tory and chalked it up to him hating Jason etc. Though I totally got that he likes Tory. She is kinda blind, but I would have been too. If there isnt some Tory-Ben romance in the next book, I'll eat the book. Without salt. And the scene near the end of the book where Ben confesses everything is soooo sweet!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I havent read any of Kathy Reichs adult books or watched Bones or anything, but this author deserves a major award, even if its just for her YA novels. I was hyperventilating in the climatic parts, and giggling maniacly in the funny part. This book rocked! I kept getting funny looks from everyone. Oh well.<br /><br />In this book, Madison gets even more evidence that Tory is a little off the normal side. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And Chance has been digging around the Parvo experiment. He is so going to find out about the Virals, if its the last thing he does. Maybe next book ,which Im assuming will be the last or second last.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> She thinks Tory is a witch. Not just like an insult, like the real thing. Magic and booyah, that kind of stuff. I noticed that Kathy Reichs co-authored this book. Why? Its spectacular, and Im not complaining, but she started the series on her own. Why start co-authoring now? EDIT: Well, it may be because I'm an idiot and didn't look in the AUTHOR column for the first book. Gah. They were all co-written. XD<br /> <br />Anyway. The way Kathy wrote the book made me feel like I was actually there. It was descriptive, and she pulled off the first-person without saying, I-did-this, I-did-that that a few authors are prone to. <br /><br />In this book , I am finally starting to comprehend the full depths of the Virals powers. They get their powers through science, which is so much more realistic and disturbing than if it was like "Oh cool! I woke up this morning and I have superpowers now!" kind of thing. The virals ease slowly into their powers, and that is creeptastic. Every single time I get sick, I start looking at my dog funny. If they started out understanding all of their powers, then it wouldnt make as much sense. <br /><br /><i> Why are there 100 pages of reviews when the book came out yesterday! Nobody will actually read this because thousands of poeple have commented on previous books and want to tell the world of goodreads that they are interested in reading this book! This is the first review Ive written, so I wanted a chance for people to see it. Which is why I chose Code as opposed to say, my fave book , The Mark of Athena by Rick Riordan. Actully, Im not sure. This might have eclipsed it. I WANT THE NEXT BOOK NOW! </i><br /><br />Of all of the characters I would most want to portray in a movie, Tory is on the top of my list. She doesnt take stuff from anyone (after the whole tripod of skank episode book 2) and she has freaking awesome superpowers!<br /><br />My only problems with this book are A) The cover. EEEW! I loved the other covers, with Tory and the gang all looking awesome! But now theyve changed the covers and it looks awful. They even changed the covers of the other books, which completely ruions my chances of ever buying one. Ick. If anyone ever finds a cover that matches the original first two, please message me or whatever so I can glue it to the front of my brand-new book. Thanks!<br />My other problem was an error on Chapter 12. Tory Flares, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ looks through Bens eyes at herself  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> goes <b> SNUP </b>, and then mentions a paragraph later that she scans the area with supersenses. Um , I thought <b> SNUP </b> meant you lost your flare, and it didnt mention restarting it. The only explanation for this is that she was yanked out of her mindbender stunt with a <b> SNUP </b>, but that doesnt really make sense. <br />Other than that, the book was absolutely awesome. Please write the next book soon Kathy &amp; Brendan! I love your writing!<br />Just change the cover for me please!<br /><br />GO VIRALS!</span>

<div id="review_479582678" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/479582678" />
    <a title="Rachel S" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5806907-rachel-s"><img alt="Rachel S" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603640746p2/5806907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/479582678?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel S" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel S" href="/user/show/5806907-rachel-s">Rachel S</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/16982426-code">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer479582678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6232892745673969079">When I first received this book through the post, I literally squealed with excitement and started dancing around my room. I'd loved the previous two books in the series - Virals and Seizure - and couldn't wait to start reading the latest instalment. And, though it was still a really great read, unfortunately, it just wasn't as good as the other two. I found a couple of faults. :(<br/><br/>I think I'll start off with the negative first. Now, when I first started reading this series, I was thirteen - a cou</span>
  <span id="freeText6232892745673969079" style="display:none">When I first received this book through the post, I literally squealed with excitement and started dancing around my room. I'd loved the previous two books in the series - Virals and Seizure - and couldn't wait to start reading the latest instalment. And, though it was still a really great read, unfortunately, it just wasn't as good as the other two. I found a couple of faults. :(<br /><br />I think I'll start off with the negative first. Now, when I first started reading this series, I was thirteen - a couple months away from my fourteenth birthday - so I was round about the same age as the main character, Tory (who was fourteen). I'm fifteen now and what I'm finding a little strange is the fact that the authors haven't really developed (or aged) the characters since the first book. Now, I know that this won't be counted as a fault to other readers, but, personally, I enjoy it a lot more when characters develop and you start seeing significant changes. But this just isn't happening for the Virals gang - they're basically the exact same as they were in the first book. <br /><br />Due to this, the one aspect in the book that I'd been hoping would progress and develop (the romance between two certain characters) just isn't happening! It's actually started to feel like it's being avoided. There's been many subtle and not-so-subtle hints throughout all three books connecting the two together but I'm still waiting for the authors to take action and, because of this, I'm getting tired of waiting. :( **SPOILER: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Those of you that have highlighted this probably know that I'm talking about BEN and Tory, right? Well, are any of you getting as frustrated as me?! I mean, it's been long enough already! However, I must say that this book probably does contain the most romance... especially nearing the end. But it isn't satisfying me enough! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.** <br /><br />Anyway. That being said, I still did thoroughly enjoy this book. Yet again, I loved the banter and witty comments between all four Virals and the type of friendship they had was sweet and enjoyable to read about. Tory still narrates very much like how a teenager speaks and her thoughts are rather relatable because of this. There are also a few chapters in third person thrown in to add effect and more development of the story from different angles and characters. I also found that, like in Seizure, I would love to have the gang as friends of my own! Their sarcasm reminds me very much of myself. ;) I don't even have a favourite as all the characters are very likeable and admirable in different ways.<br /><br />The plot line for this book was actually pretty creepy and sinister and I was quite jumpy whilst reading it! It didn't help that I was reading it at two in the morning either! I also didn't expect the culprit behind this mystery so the thrill and the need to know who it was kept me from putting it down. However, there is one twist at the end that I didn't think completely necessary. Though you won't know which one I'm talking about until you read the book! :P<br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed reading this book. Though I found the development of some aspects lacking and one of the twists nearing the end a little pointless and resulting in way more negative feelings, the characters and their relationships along with the constant mystery of who was behind it all, kept me hooked. This book also leaves you with a lot of unanswered questions and a cliffhanger that will have you eagerly - and grudgingly - waiting for book number four. I mean, I have to wait for forever for the next book now! :( I would still recommend you read this book if you have loved this series but, if you're like me, you might be a tad disappointed it wasn't quite as amazing as you'd hoped.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6232892745673969079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_275433511" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/275433511" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/275433511?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer275433511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7359196607241106778"><br/>The Reichses (permission to call them Reichs-squared, or just Reichs for this review?) do it again with another great YA novel. Having recently read and reviewed ‘Shift’, the short story by these two to bridge the previous novel to this one, I am refreshed that things have returned to normal and the hokiness found in ‘Shift’ is gone. Reichs returns with a full-on adventure that have the VIRALS tackling some very interesting and somewhat confusing clues to crack the code and solve the greater mys</span>
  <span id="freeText7359196607241106778" style="display:none"><br />The Reichses (permission to call them Reichs-squared, or just Reichs for this review?) do it again with another great YA novel. Having recently read and reviewed ‘Shift’, the short story by these two to bridge the previous novel to this one, I am refreshed that things have returned to normal and the hokiness found in ‘Shift’ is gone. Reichs returns with a full-on adventure that have the VIRALS tackling some very interesting and somewhat confusing clues to crack the code and solve the greater mystery. In true Reichs fashion, just as things seem to be wrapping up, something derails the story and takes it on another tangent. I like this… and would say the book could best some of the adult fiction I have read lately. A great story, interesting characters, and strong plot/character development that move through all three books in the series, the third installment of VIRALS is well worth a look, even for the skeptical Reichs lover.<br /><br />While YA books of this genre remind me of my early days reading choose your own adventure, Reichs injects more Adult than Young into her books and makes the bridge for mature (readers who do not usually read young adult) readers to enjoy them. Sure, there is the teenage awkwardness and the like, but the situations and language are quite mature and therefore easier to digest. Of all the mainstream adult fiction writers who have dabbled into the YA world that I read regularly (James Patterson, John Grisham, and Kathy Reichs), this is surely the best attempt, or at least the most thorough. Without knowing the true definition of the genre, it is hard to see if Reichs meets the expectations or purposely colours outside the lines.<br /><br />Well done, Madam and Mr. Reichs on this stellar book. Well worth the time for young adult and young adult reader at heart alike! Have you thought (a la ‘Shift’ of a double Brennan connection) in a Tempe Brennan book, where young Ms. Brennan has more of a role than great-aunt did? Great way to bring both sets of readers together!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7359196607241106778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9943310358423445981" style="display:none">Wut. Seriously though what the heck? Ok I'm getting ahead of myself, this book was phenomenal obviously by the rating I gave it. Kathy Reichs, you're the bomb. I've been with this series from the beginning back when I thought Virals was a stand alone. I deeply hope there is a next book to this series (she cannot possibly leave it like that). Now this book was different from the others. It was still you know the Virals taking care of business, but it was more hardcore. Which was like, whoa, this is a whole new level of crazy. There was some serious stuff going on and I didn't always like their decisions (I'm like Shelton, can we freakin' go to the police now?!) but they obviously handled it well. Now for the real talk <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ First of all Ben WTF. Like no. This is unacceptable. I totally understand Tory in the end not wanting to forgive you. I don't know that I could. I mean, you were unknowingly in cahoots with a flippin serial killer! Then you figured out he was a big fat red flag, you didn't tell your own pack!!! NO. NOT OK. And you were in a bad mood the whole book. Yes I get that it wasn't just a "bad mood" but until the end, I thought it was just petty jealousy over Jason! FYI, Ben, that is not the way to impress Tory. Piss her off, yes. Impress? WTF were you thinking. I betcha that if you would have just freakin come out and said what you felt, she would have said, "Cool, yeah I like you too, Jason just doesn't do it for me, you do. Plus you're super hot." (at least he is in my mind I mean you could fry an egg on the mental picture I've got of him) Tory never comes out and says her real feelings for Ben, but you can tell it's gonna happen. It's like Ross and Rachel, he's her lobster. But now I'm not for certain if they are going to happen because he went and mucked things up!! Holy crap she already knows you're cool Ben! You don't need to be anything else. All you needed was to TELL HER. Now you're expelled, which is stupid. And that is stressin me out. Ok rant over.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />The crime part of this book was fantastic. I had no idea what was going to happen next. It was so fun to read! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I really would never have guessed that the Gamemaker was pretending to be the forensic cop guy which the name escapes me.   <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2261658934?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vicki (The Wolf&#39;s Den)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vicki (The Wolf&#39;s Den)" href="/user/show/3911273-vicki-the-wolf-s-den">Vicki (The Wolf&#39;s Den)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18881747-code">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3911273-vicki-the-wolf-s-den?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3911273-vicki-the-wolf-s-den?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3911273-vicki-the-wolf-s-den?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3911273-vicki-the-wolf-s-den?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3911273-vicki-the-wolf-s-den?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3911273-vicki-the-wolf-s-den?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3911273-vicki-the-wolf-s-den?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2261658934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14032050329443126691">Maybe I'm getting too old for these, but I wasn't nearly as sympathetic to Tory in this book as I have been previously. I like Tory, and I get that she has a lot of drama and stress on her shoulders, but her relationships are getting awfully manipulative. <br/><br/>Even though she has no romantic interest in Jason whatsoever, she continues stringing him along just because she needs him for things. And then she gets mad at Ben for acting jealous. Ok, I can see why she wouldn't see Ben's interest in her, si</span>
  <span id="freeText14032050329443126691" style="display:none">Maybe I'm getting too old for these, but I wasn't nearly as sympathetic to Tory in this book as I have been previously. I like Tory, and I get that she has a lot of drama and stress on her shoulders, but her relationships are getting awfully manipulative. <br /><br />Even though she has no romantic interest in Jason whatsoever, she continues stringing him along just because she needs him for things. And then she gets mad at Ben for acting jealous. Ok, I can see why she wouldn't see Ben's interest in her, since her having a slight crush on him might make her overlook signals as part of her imagination. But even when things get obvious, she's hesitant to read anything into it.<br /><br />And don't even get me started on her relationships with the rest of the pack. She constantly pushes them into things they DON'T want to do, are terrified to do, but she goads them anyway. Yeah, she's the Alpha and Hi and Shelton are very timid/hesitant/scared about a lot of things, but there doesn't seem to be any empathy or trying to help them through their fears from Tory. She's very cold, calculated, and blunt. Sure, it gets the job done, but I'm starting to have second thoughts about cheering for her constantly.<br /><br />I get that Tory has a lot on her plate. She has a lot of inner turmoil to deal with about her mom, her crush(es), her relationship with Kit, highschool drama, the crazy Virals stuff, and whatever maniac is trying to kill them this week. But everything keeps being pushed back, and pushed back, and "later". I'm waiting for the explosion, and I'm getting a bit suspicious when it's taking so long to come out. <br /><br />All that being said, I did like this book in and of itself. The story was strong, the puzzles and action were on point, and the villain was a nice foil for the pack. When they're on puzzles and exploration, the story is great. When it focuses on Tory and drama... I'm getting really impatient. Sigh, teenagers. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14032050329443126691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18094169359865260220">Code by Kathy Reichs was the third installment in the Virals Series. It follows our Virals Pack as they are trying to solve the puzzles set forth by the manipulative and toxic Gamemaster. The story itself was very interesting, but many of the plot points were predictable. I liked how we seemed to see Tory grow up more, but I would have liked it much more if there wasn't the "two-boy-one-girl" romance trope. If you ignore that, I feel like the book is somewhat good. I look forward to seeing how t</span>
  <span id="freeText18094169359865260220" style="display:none">Code by Kathy Reichs was the third installment in the Virals Series. It follows our Virals Pack as they are trying to solve the puzzles set forth by the manipulative and toxic Gamemaster. The story itself was very interesting, but many of the plot points were predictable. I liked how we seemed to see Tory grow up more, but I would have liked it much more if there wasn't the "two-boy-one-girl" romance trope. If you ignore that, I feel like the book is somewhat good. I look forward to seeing how the conclusion of this book affects the next book in the series.</span>

<div id="review_636290046" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/636290046" />
    <a title="Joel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9503661-joel"><img alt="Joel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344484434p2/9503661.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/636290046?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joel" href="/user/show/9503661-joel">Joel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer636290046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14240129080970055789">Let me start by saying that on the whole, I enjoyed this book. Keep that in mind, because my review may not sound like I did.<br/><br/><em>Code</em> by Kathy and Brendan Reichs is a quite enjoyable book for the teen audience, much in the tradition of <em>The Hardy Boys</em>, <em>Nancy Drew</em>, and, for younger audiences, <em>The Boxcar Children</em>. People like their mysteries, (see television: <em>CSI</em>,<em> NCIS</em>, <em>The Mentalist</em>... if it's fiction and not a sitcom, it seems like it's mystery based) and I feel like the teen mystery really clicks wi</span>
  <span id="freeText14240129080970055789" style="display:none">Let me start by saying that on the whole, I enjoyed this book. Keep that in mind, because my review may not sound like I did.<br /><br /><em>Code</em> by Kathy and Brendan Reichs is a quite enjoyable book for the teen audience, much in the tradition of <em>The Hardy Boys</em>, <em>Nancy Drew</em>, and, for younger audiences, <em>The Boxcar Children</em>. People like their mysteries, (see television: <em>CSI</em>,<em> NCIS</em>, <em>The Mentalist</em>... if it's fiction and not a sitcom, it seems like it's mystery based) and I feel like the teen mystery really clicks with the YA audience as a whole, probably having to do with various feelings that teenagers seem to have along the lines of wanting to be smart and thinking/knowing that they're smarter than adults. That being said, it avoids two of the classic blunders of so many currently popular YA books: we don't have to deal with an overabundance of <b>Feelings</b> and it's not the evil government (true, this is more semi-fantasy than a dystopia but still... You're 14. The government doesn't care about you.) It's fun, it's fast-paced, it's funny... all in all, it's got pretty high entertainment value.<br /><br />The Reichs do a wonderful job of weaving the mystery into the lives of the Morris Island kids, and the fact that there are simultaneous storylines is part of what makes this book so enjoyable. Unfortunately, this is where the book (the series as a whole really, but it became far more pronounced for me in this book) runs into its primary issues. You see, all of the kids go to a private academy, 3 are in their Sophomore Year and one is a Junior. Unfortunately, it seems that in an effort to make the kids out to be super-geniuses, the Reichs miss the mark on making the high school believable. The kids are all in the same classes. However, they're all in Senior level classes. They are all in calculus and AP chemistry. AP chemistry is a second year course, i.e. to be taken after the student has already completed a year of chemistry, so they shouldn't be able to take it until Junior Year at the earliest. Calculus is for seniors. I know of a small set of students advanced enough to take Calculus as Juniors, but in a graduating class of 200 students maybe 3-8 fit the bill. And then these students would need to have classes to take after that. Meaning the second year of calculus (high school calculus is only the first semester of college calculus), and then likely Differential Equations. I have never heard of a high school offering Differential Equations or allowing Sophomores to take Calculus. Even if they were ready mentally and academically to take calculus, the likelihood that a high school would be willing to invest the time and man-power to develop two additional year-long courses for fewer than 10 students is <b>highly</b> unlikely.<br /><br />Now, given that these kids are super geniuses, it seems odd that there are so many things that they either don't know, or have to build from multiple sources. For example, these AP Chemistry students are trying to solve a brainteaser that contains "H2O" in sequence... and don't notice it. At all. They also don't know what a straight replacement cipher is (e.g. the Cryptoquip from the newspaper). Not all them know how longitude and latitude work. Having watched several seasons of <em>Bones</em> (though not having read any of the Temperance Brennan books, so I recognize I might be off-base here) I suspect it might have to do with the team-based approach that Kathy Reichs seems to favor. In order to give everyone a chance to shine, you've got multiple characters who have a variety of specializations, so each person gets to have a cool moment. Unfortunately, the Reichs don't seem to be sure what is or isn't common knowledge for an advanced high school student. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The kids also unsure as to whether or not the employees of LIRI should be suspects. You found the first clue hidden in a secluded area on the LIRI private island, where only LIRI personnel and guests can have free access and you don't think it's someone at LIRI... *facepalm* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Also, I don't care how much of a super-genius you are. You don't just guess the password to a flash drive someone wants protected. I had my laptop password protected and told my brother he could use it if he could figure out the password. He hasn't gotten into it in 8 years, and I've never had to change the password. If my brother, who has known me for his whole life can't figure out my password, these kids will not just happen upon the password for a Ph.D. Institute Director in fewer than 10 attempts. Not Happening.<br /><br />There is also the fact that Tory is an inconsistent narrator. In chapters/scenes where she's present, she is the clear narrative voice, speaking in the first person, and weaving her thoughts into her descriptions of actions and events where she is only an observer. However, much like the AP chemistry students don't notice H2O, her knowledge level about things seems to fluctuate at times, even within a few pages of each other. When Tory meets a contact at a firing range she says he has "Three pistols. A shotgun. Two more hunting rifles. And some automatic bullet-spitter whose name I couldn't guess." The bullet spitter turns out to be an AK-47, which is one of the more recognizable guns out there (at least in my opinion, as someone who knows next to nothing about guns). A page later the contact "lifted his Beretta 9mm." ... So Tory can't recognize an AK, but can identify a specific model of pistol, that looks like most other pistols? There are other examples, but I suppose a few of them could be chalked up to exaggeration on her part (e.g. she claims to not be able to name more than two fashion designers, and then in a fit of clever narration drops the name of 2 designers having already mentioned at least one earlier in the chapter [sorry, I can't find the exact quotation]). <br /><br />In the end though, I've come to realize that I just don't like Tory. She's hypocritical, shallow, misogynistic, deceitful, and routinely breaks promises. She rails against the bullies for Bolton Prep for calling her and her friends "boat people" since they have to commute by boat from a rural island, but she and her friends utilize the term "redneck" on more than one occasion. She also convinces Shelton to stay at a drinking party, and possibly peer-pressures him into drinking (I already returned the book, so I can't reread this section to verify whether she pressures him into drinking or just staying at the party), and then criticizes her friends for drinking at this party while she doesn't. The problem with this is that the only reason she doesn't drink is that she has a PTSD-esque flashback to the cops notifying her that her mom was killed by a drunk driver. She backs out because of emotional scarring, not because she thinks underage drinking is wrong. Then we get the big surprise that it's totally okay with the "cool kids" that she doesn't drink! Except that the party's host is a social-elite lacrosse player and has a crush on her, and so he is willing to overlook it. She's also not opposed to drinking to excess, as she plays drinking games, but has said host cover her losses, thereby accelerating his rate of intoxication. So, no, she didn't drink, but I don't really think she has a leg to stand on when she tries to criticize her friends for getting drunk at the party that she brought them to, either.<br /><br />Tory's misogyny and shallowness seem to go hand in hand in trying to make Tory a particular type of person: a smart science girl, that's still a teenager. Tory does not like a single other female character. In fact, she seems to hate <b>every</b> other female she encounters. They are all "bimbos" and "bitches." In some cases, the major offense seems to be that they dress like the prototypical woman. But you can be into science, and still want to be fashionable. As someone who has a Bachelor's Degree in physics, I met several female students whose majors were physics, biology, chemistry, mathematics or engineering, and they still dressed like the majority of the female student population. It's not a binary system where you can either be a math-sci person or you can be socially/fashionably savvy. It's also strange to me that she hates all other females, since even the women that I've known who were primarily friends with men did not have zero same gender friends. In fact, they usually had at least one friend who was also a woman that they were closer to than they were to all of their male friends. The fact that Tory is more comfortable with the male population in general doesn't exclude her from being able to be friends with another girl. And the source of her disdain for women clearly can't be that these other women objectify men, because she does too! Here are some of her descriptions of her classmate, Chance: "Chance was gorgeous, refined, and genteel. Sculpted like a gladiator with the manner of a prince." and "Dark skin, dark eyes, and dark humor. His thick black hair framed strong features and a Hollywood perfect chin. Tall, slender, and muscular without being bulky. In a word, he was gorgeous." During the reader's first encounter with a department head at LIRI, Anders Sundberg, is described as "easily LIRI's most handsome employee. Just a shade past thirty, a former Olympic swimmer, he looked like a taller, buffer Justin Timberlake. In other words, pretty hot." (Side note, here again, I feel like we lessen verisimilitude for the sake of being impressive. To me "a shade past thirty" would be 30-32ish. To get a Ph.D. in marine biology would probably take 5-6 years past a Bachelor's Degree, so he probably wouldn't finish it until he was 28 or so, especially since he probably doesn't have enough time to take extra classes to finish faster since he's training for the Olympics. Which would leave him 2-4 years to not only build up the credentials to get hired at this super prestigious research facility, but also to then be chosen as a department chair within his first 2-3 years. It really doesn't seem plausible. But I digress...) To me, it seems that all of this is trying to make Tory into a role model for young women to get interested in science. */See? You can be smart and like math and science, but still be a normal teenage girl that has normal feelings towards physically attractive males!/* <br /><br />The deceit and promise breaking go hand in hand as well. The deceit I'm almost willing to overlook, since it's somewhat integral to the plot. */Gee, Dad, I've got wolf-based super powers, and if I don't regularly sneak out, a crazed psychopath who already blew up a gazebo in a popular park will likely commit another act of terrorism./* Yeah, I could see how that wouldn't fly. However, she promised on more than one occasion not to use the magic wolf powers to tap into the minds of her friends without permission, and she breaks that promise on multiple occasions. I mean, in other sci-fi/fantasy books where telepathy is possible that has been described as being tantamount to rape. <br /><br />Really, what it all boils down to is that Tory is "special." She is a Dostoyevskian Superman. Because she's smart, attractive (but not a bimbo), and has superpowers, she is above social conventions, general ethics, and rules. Even one of the teachers at Bolton Prep says so, when he makes an exception for her to be allowed to leave detention since she's one of Bolton's brightest students, and shouldn't be there in the first place. Just because a student does well academically does not mean that they follow all of the rules of the institution. (After lying her way out of mid-day detention to go use her cell phone, she then skips school altogether to go meet a contact.) I don't like the concept of the Superman, and the more I think about it, the more I think this is one of the main sources for my disdain for Tory Brennan.<br /><br />All in all, it is a truly fun book, and aside from a few other details (e.g. the wolf thinks in English word fragments, the 3 books up to this point take place over a 6-8 month span, but reference things that are popular during their publication years which is a course of 3 years) I greatly enjoyed myself. Much like I watch <em>Bones</em> for the secondary characters and not Temperance Brennan, I will continue to read the <em>Virals</em> series for the story and side characters, and not for Tory.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14240129080970055789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2667046621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4346382840049549104">OH MY GOD.. this book is definitely my favorite in the series by far. The ending chapter was amazing and I don't want to say because of spoilers but, dammmmmmmmm I want to start reading the next book right now. The story amazing and the character development absolutely a 10/10. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7744611.Code__Virals___3_' title='Code (Virals, #3) by Kathy Reichs' rel='nofollow noopener'>Code</a> was definitely outstanding and had an ending that I didn't expect. This tale was full of excitement and it really made you think! Again as I have said million times, it has been holidays so i wanted to ready like str</span>
  <span id="freeText4346382840049549104" style="display:none">OH MY GOD.. this book is definitely my favorite in the series by far. The ending chapter was amazing and I don't want to say because of spoilers but, dammmmmmmmm I want to start reading the next book right now. The story amazing and the character development absolutely a 10/10. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7744611.Code__Virals___3_" title="Code (Virals, #3) by Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Code</a> was definitely outstanding and had an ending that I didn't expect. This tale was full of excitement and it really made you think! Again as I have said million times, it has been holidays so i wanted to ready like stream train but with, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7744611.Code__Virals___3_" title="Code (Virals, #3) by Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Code</a> i had no choice, I just couldn't put it down. One thing that I really loved about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7744611.Code__Virals___3_" title="Code (Virals, #3) by Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Code</a> was how that story was just so elaborate. Another thing also is that the story wasn't what I was expecting it to be, like, Omg how did <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26372.Kathy_Reichs" title="Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Kathy Reichs</a> think of this, a Game coordinated by a crazy man, wow. It's absolutely my favorite in the series so far. I was really amazed at how the characters themselves changed but especially Ben, Tory, and Kit like just wow. And an update yes... I still definitely have been <i> dreaming </i> about being infected by a virus and then obtaining supernatural abilities. But now I find pirate treasure and get put in a game where I have to get out but the only way to get out is by solving riddles and stuff like that.<br /><br />So yee, next time I will see you is when I have hopefully completed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19034958.Swipe__Virals___3_5_" title="Swipe (Virals, #3.5) by Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Swipe</a> the short story between <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7744611.Code__Virals___3_" title="Code (Virals, #3) by Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Code</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17999135.Exposure__Virals___4_" title="Exposure (Virals, #4) by Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Exposure</a>.<br /><br />once again... I really enjoyed something a little different from what I normally read, and I'm super excited to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19034958.Swipe__Virals___3_5_" title="Swipe (Virals, #3.5) by Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Swipe</a> next!<br />Thank you <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26372.Kathy_Reichs" title="Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Kathy Reichs</a>, for making <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7800188.Virals__Virals___1_" title="Virals (Virals, #1) by Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Virals</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8709640.Seizure__Virals___2_" title="Seizure (Virals, #2) by Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Seizure</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24368550.Shock__Virals___0_5_" title="Shock (Virals, #0.5) by Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Shock</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17472970.Shift__Virals___2_5_" title="Shift (Virals, #2.5) by Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Shift</a> and now <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7744611.Code__Virals___3_" title="Code (Virals, #3) by Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Code</a> a great adventure that I could become apart of.<br /><br />Sincerely <br />Nate</span>
  <a data-text-id="4346382840049549104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText10533714604963374136" style="display:none">Freakishly amazing. <br />Awesomely horrifying. <br />And I think the felony count was only four this time. Though being scolded by a monk was definitely a new one.<br />Everything's at an all-time high in Reichs' "Code".         <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3438977158" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14671758144998624268">I enjoyed this book, but, even though it is a sci-fi YA novel, some of this stretches believability. The first book happens and then six months later we are working on our third adventure (including the first book). No way these kids' parents let them out of the house after the first book! lol The book drags a bit in the middle, but it ends really well. Reichs develops really believable characters, and the main characters are a very believable group of teenagers that naturally includes a multipl</span>
  <span id="freeText14671758144998624268" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book, but, even though it is a sci-fi YA novel, some of this stretches believability. The first book happens and then six months later we are working on our third adventure (including the first book). No way these kids' parents let them out of the house after the first book! lol The book drags a bit in the middle, but it ends really well. Reichs develops really believable characters, and the main characters are a very believable group of teenagers that naturally includes a multiplicity of ethnicities. The characters don't feel forced or like they are tropes or stereotypes at all. They are very authentic kids. I feel like I have known each of those kids at some point. This is one of Reichs strong suits in these novels. It is a pretty good YA read with real characters who encounter some fantastical problems. You should check it out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14671758144998624268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Katelyn Brennan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/107780330-katelyn-brennan"><img alt="Katelyn Brennan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578866440p2/107780330.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/107780330-katelyn-brennan?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/107780330-katelyn-brennan?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/107780330-katelyn-brennan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,
