        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3225719578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1554169629010259141"><b>Age:</b> 13+<br/><b>Trigger Warnings:</b> Violence, murder, attempted murder, morally gray concepts, language<br/><b>Library Category:</b> YA (Mystery)<br/><br/><b>Overview:</b> I really love this series. The concept is intriguing and the execution engaging - it's well-written and has good character development. The only thing I didn't like was the lack of morality. The main characters just seemed to do whatever they felt like doing, even if it involved criminal acts, without much thought to the repercussions of their actions. They never r</span>
  <span id="freeText1554169629010259141" style="display:none"><b>Age:</b> 13+<br /><b>Trigger Warnings:</b> Violence, murder, attempted murder, morally gray concepts, language<br /><b>Library Category:</b> YA (Mystery)<br /><br /><b>Overview:</b> I really love this series. The concept is intriguing and the execution engaging - it's well-written and has good character development. The only thing I didn't like was the lack of morality. The main characters just seemed to do whatever they felt like doing, even if it involved criminal acts, without much thought to the repercussions of their actions. They never really received any punishment, either.<br /><br />On a side note, I also really enjoyed the side plot of the debutantes and their festivities. It added an extra layer, which made Tory's character really come to life.<br /><br /><b>Possibly offensive content:</b> Again, the lack of morality may bother some readers. There was some language, and the whole story was based upon a psychotic murderer, so obviously there was violence and death.<br /><br />I would definitely recommend this series, especially to teens that love action-packed mysteries.</span>

<div id="review_559428942" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/559428942" />
    <a title="Kenzii" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18116531-kenzii"><img alt="Kenzii" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375303264p2/18116531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/559428942?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kenzii" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kenzii" href="/user/show/18116531-kenzii">Kenzii</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERYONE</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kenzii by: </span>
      My amazing intuition
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer559428942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6633890622970817864"><i>What did you think?</i> Goodreads asks me. <br/><br/>HOLY. I CAN'T EVEN.<br/><br/><b>THIS WILL HAVE LOTS OF SPOILERS BECAUSE I JUST NEED TO TALK ABOUT IT!!!!! YOU HAVE BEEN WARNED!</b><br/><br/>This has got to be the best one yet. Tory is still as bad as ever, the boys are still as smoking and funny, and-<br/><br/>WOAH. Who saw that ending!?!?!?!? My heart shattered in two when I found out...<a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Ben...oh Ben...how could you? <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br/><br/>Anyways, the plot was amazing. I think it's the best one yet. Basic summary: Hiram and Shelton </span>
  <span id="freeText6633890622970817864" style="display:none"><i>What did you think?</i> Goodreads asks me. <br /><br />HOLY. I CAN'T EVEN.<br /><br /><b>THIS WILL HAVE LOTS OF SPOILERS BECAUSE I JUST NEED TO TALK ABOUT IT!!!!! YOU HAVE BEEN WARNED!</b><br /><br />This has got to be the best one yet. Tory is still as bad as ever, the boys are still as smoking and funny, and-<br /><br />WOAH. Who saw that ending!?!?!?!? My heart shattered in two when I found out...<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ben...oh Ben...how could you? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Anyways, the plot was amazing. I think it's the best one yet. Basic summary: Hiram and Shelton are snooping around, looking for a cache that was posted on a website and was reported to be buried on Loggerhead. They find it, and on it is an invitation to "play the game." And it is signed by the "Gamemaster." They follow the clues, which leads them to Castle Pickney, and then the game turns deadly, when a bomb goes off in Battery Park. The Gamemaster requires them to continue to play the game, follow his rules, or else innocents will die, inlcuding their loved ones. Left with no choice, the Virals set off on a mission to save a whole bunch of unsuspecting, innocent people.<br /><br />The writing was as clever and quick as always. I just love the way Kathy Reichs writes. I love the way she builds her characters. These books have some of the best male characters I've ever read about. These boys are funny, smart, <i>respectful</i> (imagine that) and Ms. Reichs lets us get to learn about their likes, dislikes, hobbies and fears. They aren't cardboard cut outs that do nothing but add sex appeal to the book. They are real.<br /><br />Tory is drawn so well, too. You can really see her character growth through out the books. I feel so bad for her when Kit announces that Whitney will move in with them. She has so much going on, the pain of her mother's death is still fresh, now her father's girlfriend might move in, and on top of that she's trying to save innocent people from being murdered by a maniac. However, in the first book, there was nothing but hatred for Whitney. In the third book, you can see that she has grown a bit softer and more tolerant, which is nice to see. (Also, I kind of like Whitney...I don't know why. She reminds me of Effie from The Hunger Games.)<br /><br />Speaking of Kit, who saw that at the end!?!?! Way to go, Dad! <br /><br />The science is very well written. I learn a lot from these books. (It's quite helpful, as I am currently taking a forensic science course. So now, when I get to certain lectures in the course, say about identifying the sex and age of a skelton, I think <i>BAM. Already knew that!</i>)<br /><br />Anyways...<br /><br />Cooper being the center of power for the Virals was really neat. I thought it was really cool to keep on including him in the stories. After all, he was the one who gave them their powers. To discard him would be unfair. <br /><br />Also, the mind reading!? That was awesome! It's just so...unnatural! But it was well written and fit in really well with the story.<br /><br />The story was amzing. I was laughing every single time Hiram said something. And then it would get funnier when Shelton added something. These boys are seriously the best characters ever. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'd love a book from Hi's point of view, Kathy Reichs. Just sayin'... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Oh but the ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ben. I know you liked her and wanted her to notice you. But seriously...that was a little extreme. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I know that a lot of people will not like how this ended. Ben made a lot of mistakes, but at least he can man up and take responsibility for his mistakes. Ben, you are a real man.<br /><br />I could go on and on and on and on about how awesome this books is. But please do yourself a favor and read this book. I order you to. You won't regret it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6633890622970817864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_655310570" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/655310570" />
    <a title="Kelsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10407130-kelsey"><img alt="Kelsey" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/655310570?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelsey" href="/user/show/10407130-kelsey">Kelsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer655310570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17099757782629850367">What I Think: I need to start by saying that I'm a very big fan of Kathy Reichs so I may be bias. I think that she is a great writer and I always enjoy reading her novels especially her young adult novels because they still require thought but are at a level that are easy to understand and easy to read. They make you feel like you are getting the science of a more hardcore novel but are still able to enjoy the drama of teenage life. It mixes two of my favourite things. I was however very dissapo</span>
  <span id="freeText17099757782629850367" style="display:none">What I Think: I need to start by saying that I'm a very big fan of Kathy Reichs so I may be bias. I think that she is a great writer and I always enjoy reading her novels especially her young adult novels because they still require thought but are at a level that are easy to understand and easy to read. They make you feel like you are getting the science of a more hardcore novel but are still able to enjoy the drama of teenage life. It mixes two of my favourite things. I was however very dissapointed with the cover change. Now my set doesn't match. OCD FTW? I think this one should match, how hard is that?<br /><br />Anyway, I digress! I love the setting of this series. The authors paint a beautiful picture of the area and allow me to visualize what the characters are seeing. That helps to get me into the story. It's a great place for these stories to take place too. I couldn't imagine how different it would be if it took place elsewhere. I'm happy that it doesn't.<br /><br />The characters are great. They are each unique. Kit is as far away and still close as ever. He is more aware then is let on until the end. I feel like he gets ignored too often. He's a great guy. Whitney...urg! I'd kill her if I were Tory. God bless Tory for not killing her. Tory is a great leader. I like that she tests limits but also realizes the need to be safe. She is also compassionate and worries about hurting the feelings of other people. It's the perfect mix of what people feel. Everything is tossed inside but at different levels. She has the depth of a true person. However, she should have figured out what was what between Ben and Jason. <br /><br />I love the snappy writing and the small, quick jokes. I am sarcastic and relate to that well. This book gives a few good laughs while keeping itself honest and true to the characters and story line. Tension is released at the best moments and built when it needs to be. Emotions ran to fit the story; I got into it. I was upset at the end just as Tory was and I felt betrayed and hurt and happy like she did. Mostly, I felt bad that she had to put up with so much creepy. The biggest creep (in this story) being for a stupid reason in the end. Though, to level with you, I figured out what was going on before I got to the end. I also figured out quite a few of the puzzles which made me angry because if I could figure it out, why couldn't they? I should have been proud but I was just disappointed. The feeling didn't last though.<br /><br />In Conclusion:I could see myself reading this novel again in the future. As I said before, I am a big fan of Kathy Reichs. I have all her novels and, of them, this series is definitely the easiest to follow. I enjoyed the quick wit, quick read, and small bites of science. If you like crime, puzzles, and mystery you might like this novel. However, it's not all true science since they are Virals. Science-fiction gets thrown into the mix so if you don't enjoy that beware. Me? I'm waiting for the next book.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://one-chapter-ahead.blogspot.ca/">http://one-chapter-ahead.blogspot.ca/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17099757782629850367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KDrNyzY0duwVhgWaHblpeB7JOlzaA/yescaSH404hAxrB0uKN0LmxTK0KiaK2lu/dnvqdBGEteZl1I14uk9DvQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xVAakLfjN3cwacp9u6ZSxE/dZA+GpJCfvD45FJQF9kuGbZzRtpWnXhdb5cEsxWADJ2+0J00j2edoLCZzo3Ix+g==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer1807783157238508168">Kathy Reichs is a forensic anthropologist for the Office of the Chief Medical Examiner, State of North Carolina, and for the Laboratoire des Sciences Judiciaires et de Médecine Légale for the province of Quebec. She is one of only fifty forensic anthropologists certified by the American Board of Forensic Anthropology and is on the Board of Directors of the American Academy of Forensic Sciences. A </span>
  <span id="freeText1807783157238508168" style="display:none">Kathy Reichs is a forensic anthropologist for the Office of the Chief Medical Examiner, State of North Carolina, and for the Laboratoire des Sciences Judiciaires et de Médecine Légale for the province of Quebec. She is one of only fifty forensic anthropologists certified by the American Board of Forensic Anthropology and is on the Board of Directors of the American Academy of Forensic Sciences. A professor of anthropology at The University of North Carolina at Charlotte, Dr. Reichs is a native of Chicago, where she received her Ph.D. at Northwestern. She now divides her time between Charlotte and Montreal and is a frequent expert witness in criminal trials.<br /><br /><b>Awards:</b><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/award/show/1066-arthur-ellis-award" rel="nofollow noopener">Arthur Ellis Award</a><br />◊ Best First Novel (1998): Deja Dead</span>
